<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background:#ccc">Rape</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tizian_094.jpg"><img alt="Tizian 094.jpg" data-file-height="3440" data-file-width="2514" height="411" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Tizian_094.jpg/300px-Tizian_094.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Tizian_094.jpg/450px-Tizian_094.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Tizian_094.jpg/600px-Tizian_094.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">The rape of noblewoman <a href="/wiki/Lucretia" title="Lucretia">Lucretia</a> was a starting point of events that led to the overthrow of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Kingdom" title="Roman Kingdom">Roman Kingdom</a> and establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. As a direct result of rape, Lucretia committed <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a>. Many artists and writers were inspired by the story, including <a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_Lucrece" title="The Rape of Lucrece">Shakespeare</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Lucretia_(Botticelli)" title="The Story of Lucretia (Botticelli)">Botticelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht Dürer">Dürer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artemisia_Gentileschi" title="Artemisia Gentileschi">Artemisia Gentileschi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Heywood" title="Thomas Heywood">Thomas Heywood</a>.</td>
</tr>

<p><b>Rape</b> is a type of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexual assault</a> usually involving <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a> or other forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_penetration" title="Sexual penetration">sexual penetration</a> perpetrated against a person without that person's <a href="/wiki/Consent" title="Consent">consent</a>. The act may be carried out by physical force, <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_and_control_in_abusive_relationships" title="Power and control in abusive relationships">abuse of authority</a> or against a person who is incapable of giving valid consent, such as one who is unconscious, incapacitated, has an <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_disability" title="Intellectual disability">intellectual disability</a> or is below the legal <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who.int_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictionary.reference.com_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-dictionary.reference.com-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefreedictionary.com_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefreedictionary.com-3">[3]</a></sup> The term <i>rape</i> is sometimes used interchangeably with the term <i>sexual assault.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rate of reporting, prosecuting and convicting for rape varies between jurisdictions. Internationally, the incidence of rapes recorded by the police during 2008 ranged, per 100,000 people, from 0.2 in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> to 92.9 in <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> with 6.3 in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unodc1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-unodc1-5">[5]</a></sup> Rape by strangers is usually less common than rape by persons the victim knows, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rape_of_males_by_males" title="Rape of males by males">male-on-male</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesbian_rape" title="Lesbian rape">female-on-female</a> <a href="/wiki/Prison_rape" title="Prison rape">prison rapes</a> are common and may be the least reported forms of rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Widespread and systematic rape and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_slavery" title="Sexual slavery">sexual slavery</a> can occur during international conflict. These practices are <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a>. Rape is also recognized as an element of the crime of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> when committed with the intent to destroy, in whole or in part, a targeted ethnic group.</p>
<p>People who have been raped can be <a href="/wiki/Psychological_trauma" title="Psychological trauma">traumatized</a> and develop <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaets_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-aaets-9">[9]</a></sup> Serious injuries can result along with the risk of <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infection" title="Sexually transmitted infection">sexually transmitted infections</a>. A person may face violence or threats from the rapist, and, in some cultures, from the victim's family and relatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zeenews.india_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-zeenews.india-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wisemuslimwomen_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-wisemuslimwomen-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The term <i>rape</i> originates in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/rapere" title="wikt:Special:Search/rapere"><i>rapere</i></a> (supine stem <i>raptum</i>), "to snatch, to grab, to carry off".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cor_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-cor-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kei_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kei-14">[14]</a></sup> Since the 14th century, the term has come to mean "to seize and take away by force".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-merriam-webster.com_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-merriam-webster.com-15">[15]</a></sup> In Roman law the carrying off of a woman by force, with or without intercourse, constituted "raptus".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kei_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kei-14">[14]</a></sup> In Medieval English law the same term could refer to either kidnapping or rape in the modern sense of "sexual violation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cor_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-cor-13">[13]</a></sup> The original meaning of "carry off by force" is still found in some phrases, such as "rape and pillage" or in titles, such as the stories of the <a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_the_Sabine_Women" title="The Rape of the Sabine Women">Rape of the Sabine Women</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">The Rape of Europa</a> or the poem <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_the_Lock" title="The Rape of the Lock">The Rape of the Lock</a></i>, which is about the theft of a lock of hair.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Types_of_rape" title="Types of rape">Types of rape</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laws_regarding_rape" title="Laws regarding rape">Laws regarding rape</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rape_by_gender" title="Rape by gender">Rape by gender</a></div>
<p>Rape is defined in most jurisdictions as <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a>, or other forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_penetration" title="Sexual penetration">sexual penetration</a>, initiated by a perpetrator against a victim without their <a href="/wiki/Consent" title="Consent">consent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book04_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Book04-16">[16]</a></sup> The definition of rape is inconsistent between governmental health organizations, law enforcement, health providers and legal professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maier2008_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maier2008-17">[17]</a></sup> It has varied historically and culturally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book04_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Book04-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maier2008_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maier2008-17">[17]</a></sup> Originally, <i>rape</i> had no sexual connotation and is still used in other contexts in English. In <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a>, it or <i>raptus</i> was classified as a form of <i>crimen vis</i>, "crime of assault".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <i>Raptus</i> described the abduction of a woman against the will of the man under whose authority she lived, and sexual intercourse was not a necessary element. Other definitions of rape have changed over time. In 1940, a husband could not be charged with raping his wife. In the 1950s, in some states, a white woman having consensual sex with a black man was considered rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI) still considered rape a crime solely committed by men against women. In 2012, they changed their definition from "The carnal knowledge of a female forcibly and against her will" to "The penetration, no matter how slight, of the vagina or anus with any body part or object, or <a href="/wiki/Oral_sex" title="Oral sex">oral penetration</a> by a sex organ of another person, without the consent of the victim." The previous definition, which had remained unchanged since 1927, was considered outdated and narrow. The updated definition includes recognizing any gender of victim and perpetrator and that rape with an object can be as traumatic as penile/vaginal rape. The bureau further describes instances when the victim is unable to give consent because of mental or physical incapacity. It recognizes that a victim can be incapacitated by drugs and alcohol and unable to consent. The definition does not change federal or state criminal codes or impact charging and prosecution on the federal, state or local level; it rather means that rape will be more accurately reported nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Health organizations and agencies have also expanded rape beyond traditional definitions. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) defines rape as a form of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexual assault</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2002-23">[23]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC) includes rape in their definition of sexual assault; they term rape a form of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a>. The CDC lists other acts of coercive, non-consensual sexual activity that may or may not include rape, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug-facilitated_sexual_assault" title="Drug-facilitated sexual assault">drug-facilitated sexual assault</a>, acts in which a victim is made to penetrate a perpetrator or someone else, intoxication where the victim is unable to consent (due to incapacitation or being unconscious), non-physically forced penetration which occurs after a person is pressured verbally (by intimidation or misuse of authority to force to consent), or completed or attempted forced penetration of a victim via unwanted physical force (including using a weapon or threatening to use a weapon).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovchick2016_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Markovchick2016-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some countries or jurisdictions differentiate between rape and sexual assault by defining rape as involving penile penetration of the vagina, or solely penetration involving the penis, while other types of non-consensual sexual activity are called sexual assault.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalbfleisch_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalbfleisch-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plummer_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plummer-27">[27]</a></sup> Scotland, for example, emphasizes penile penetration, requiring that the sexual assault must have been committed by use of a penis to qualify as rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legislation.gov.uk.2C_rape_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-legislation.gov.uk.2C_rape-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News.2C_rape_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News.2C_rape-29">[29]</a></sup> In some instances, as in the case of Germany, penetration is not required for the act to be defined as rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book04_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Book04-16">[16]</a></sup> The 1998 <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_Rwanda" title="International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda">International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda</a> defines rape as "a physical invasion of a sexual nature committed on a person under circumstances which are coercive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book04_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Book04-16">[16]</a></sup> In other cases, the term <i>rape</i> has been phased out of legal use in favor of terms such as <i>sexual assault</i> or <i>criminal sexual conduct</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Some laws have eliminated the term <i>rape</i> altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope">Scope</span></h3>
<p>For research purposes, incidence of rapes are classified into a number of categories. These can be <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a>, age, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnicity" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographical_location" title="Geographical location">geographical location</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> or historical periods. Other categories of rape describe the relationship of the perpetrator to the victim and the context of the sexual assault. Rape is categorized as <a href="/wiki/Date_rape" title="Date rape">date rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gang_rape" title="Gang rape">gang rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape" title="Marital rape">marital rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incestual rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prison_rape" title="Prison rape">prison rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acquaintance_rape" title="Acquaintance rape">acquaintance rape</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_rape" title="War rape">war rape</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statutory_rape" title="Statutory rape">statutory rape</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Victims of rape or sexual assault come from a wide range of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientations</a>, genders, ages, and degrees of impairment or disability. Perpetrators sometimes use objects for penetration, force the victim to penetrate the perpetrator, force the victim to perform oral sex or assault the victim with anal penetration. Those experiencing non-consensual, forced sexual experiences and sexual assault include women, heterosexual men, homosexual men, boys, adolescent males, spouses, girlfriends, boyfriends, prepubescent girls and boys, adolescent girls, children, the elderly, and even infants. Forced sexual experiences can be committed over a long period of time accompanied with little to no physical injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosdahl_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rosdahl-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelly2011_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kelly2011-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an early study of U.S. 1,632 students from 79 different schools, boys and girls were surveyed and asked if they had, at some time, been asked to engage in unwelcome sexual behavior. 85% of the girls and 76% of the boys said that this had occurred. The boys and girls indicated that the behavior they experienced included pinching, grabbing, touching in a sexual manner. One fourth of the girls had been forced to kiss someone and 10% of both the girls and the boys reported having been forced against their wills to do something sexual other than kissing. Students reported that 80% of the unwelcome sexual behavior had come from other students with the remainder coming from teachers, coaches, or other adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelly2011_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kelly2011-34">[34]</a></sup> Out of the total of child abuse rates, slightly more than 75% were neglected, 18% were assaulted and slightly more than nine percent were sexually abused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consent">Consent</span></h3>
<p>Lack of consent is key to the definition of rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefreedictionary.com_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-thefreedictionary.com-3">[3]</a></sup> Consent is not always expressed verbally. It may be implied from the context and from the relationship of the parties, but the absence of objection does not of itself constitute consent. Lack of consent may result from either forcible compulsion by the perpetrator or an incapacity to consent on the part of the victim (such as persons who are asleep, intoxicated or otherwise mentally compromised).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-36">[36]</a></sup> Sexual intercourse with a person below the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a>, i.e., the age at which legal competence is established, is referred to as statutory rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefreedictionary.com_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-thefreedictionary.com-3">[3]</a></sup> In certain jurisdictions, consent may also be negated if an individual agrees to have sex only on certain terms. An example is the case of a man who deliberately ejaculated in a woman's vagina although she consented to sex only on the clear understanding that he would not do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Consent can be withdrawn at any time, so that any further sexual activity would constitute rape.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duress" title="Duress">Duress</a> is the situation when the person is threatened by overwhelming force or violence, and may result in the absence of an objection to intercourse. This can lead to the presumption of consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-36">[36]</a></sup> Duress may be actual or threatened force or violence against the victim or someone close to the victim. Even <a href="/wiki/Blackmail" title="Blackmail">blackmail</a> may constitute duress. <a href="/wiki/Abuse_of_power" title="Abuse of power">Abuse of power</a> may constitute duress. For instance, in the Philippines, a man commits rape if he engages in sexual intercourse with a woman <i>"By means of fraudulent machination or grave abuse of authority"</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda in its landmark 1998 judgment used a definition of rape which did not use the word 'consent': "a physical invasion of a sexual nature committed on a person <i>under circumstances which are coercive</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Marital rape, or spousal rape, is non-consensual sex in which the perpetrator is the victim's spouse. It is a form of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_by_intimate_partners" title="Sexual violence by intimate partners">partner rape</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, and of sexual abuse. Once widely accepted or ignored by law, spousal rape is now denounced by international conventions and is increasingly criminalized. Still, in many countries, spousal rape either remains legal, or is illegal but widely tolerated and accepted as a husband's prerogative. In 2006, the UN Secretary-General's <i>In-depth study on all forms of violence against women</i> stated that (pg 113): "Marital rape may be prosecuted in at least 104 States. Of these, 32 have made marital rape a specific criminal offence, while the remaining 74 do not exempt marital rape from general rape provisions. Marital rape is not a prosecutable offence in at least 53 States. Four States criminalize marital rape only when the spouses are judicially separated. Four States are considering legislation that would allow marital rape to be prosecuted."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Since 2006, several other states have outlawed marital rape (for example <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> in 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>). In the US, the criminalization of marital rape started in the mid-1970s and in 1993 North Carolina became the last state to make marital rape illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In many countries, it is not clear if marital rape may or may not be prosecuted under ordinary rape laws. In the absence of a spousal rape law, it may be possible to bring prosecution for acts of forced sexual intercourse inside marriage by prosecuting, through the use of other criminal offenses (such as assault based offenses), the acts of violence or criminal threat that were used to obtain submission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The issues of consent in sexual situations can be complicated by language, context, culture and sexual orientation. Refusal or lack of consent is interpreted by cultural expectations of women. A common view is that a woman's refusal of sex cannot be 'heard' in strict patriarchal culture. If a culture depersonalizes and sexualizes women, the refusal and non-consensual, verbalized 'no' to sex can be distorted and instead means 'keep trying', or even 'yes'. In this context, men are able to sincerely claim they did not understand the refusal. Women can then be blamed because they did not communicate their lack of consent clearly enough. When bruises or broken bones are not apparent, this is seen as proof that the woman consented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulick2003_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kulick2003-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In other contexts, men never say 'no' when confronted with female pressure to engage in sex. In this same situation the lack of consent would be a threat and identify him as homosexual. If the man unwillingly engages in sex, this can create an unusual situation in which the man must defend his claim by highlighting the physical unattractiveness of the female. Interestingly, situations like this can progress to one where continued interaction can prolong the encounter in hopes of reversing non-consent to a 'yes'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulick2003_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kulick2003-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Investigations into questions regarding the intentions behind non-consensual sex are sparse. One investigation in the early 1980s questioned 610 undergraduate women. They were asked if they had ever said no to sex, even though they fully intended to have sexual intercourse. The majority, 68.5% of these women answered 'no' when their intention was 'maybe'. The other 39.3% answered that when they have said 'no' really meant 'yes'. The explanations in support of their answers were that they were fearful of being considered promiscuous. Some claimed they were inhibited about sex. Others answered that they intended to manipulate the male because they were angry, wanted him to become more aroused or more aggressive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulick2003_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kulick2003-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Context changes again when a man solicits sex from another man. Some stereotypes identify men who 'pursue' other men are the most virile of all. This type of interaction often becomes erotic in nature and now can be interpreted as an invitation. Conversely, unwanted sexual advances have created a legal precedent: Homosexual Panic Defense. This is invoked when a man who has murdered another man who they claim made sexual advances towards them. This is an argument in which a sexual advance itself is an act of aggression, and that the defendant was justified in using violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulick2003_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kulick2003-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motives">Motives</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_sexual_violence" title="Causes of sexual violence">Causes of sexual violence</a></div>
<p>The WHO states that the principal factors that lead to the perpetration of sexual violence against women, including rape, are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>beliefs in family honor and sexual purity;</li>
<li>ideologies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Male_entitlement" title="Male entitlement">male sexual entitlement</a>;</li>
<li>weak legal sanctions for sexual violence.</li>
</ul>
<p>No single theory explains the motivation for rape; the motives of rapists can be multi-factorial. Several factors have been proposed: <a href="/wiki/Anger" title="Anger">anger</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_(philosophy)" title="Power (philosophy)">power</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sexual_sadism_disorder" title="Sexual sadism disorder">sadism</a>; sexual gratification in tandem with <a href="/wiki/Sociobiological_theories_of_rape" title="Sociobiological theories of rape">evolutionary proclivities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinical_psychologist" title="Clinical psychologist">clinical psychologist</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Lisak" title="David Lisak">David Lisak</a>, co-author of a 2002 study of undetected rapists,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> says that compared with non-rapists, both undetected and convicted rapists are measurably more angry at women and more motivated by a desire to dominate and control them, are more impulsive, disinhibited, anti-social, hyper-masculine, and less empathic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sexual aggression is often perceived as masculine identity characteristic of manhood in some male groups and is significantly correlated to the desire to be held higher in esteem among male peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Sexually aggressive behavior among young men has been correlated with gang or group membership as well as having other delinquent peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ouimette_PC_1998_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ouimette_PC_1998-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borowsky_IW_1997_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Borowsky_IW_1997-53">[53]</a></sup> Research also suggests that men with sexually aggressive peers have a higher chance of reporting coercive or forced sexual intercourse outside gang circles than men without such sexually aggressive peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Gang rape is often perceived by male perpetrators as a justified method to discourage or punish what they consider as immoral behavior among women for example wearing short skirts or visiting bars. In some areas in <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, women can actually be punished by public gang rape usually through permission by elders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jenkins_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jenkins-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span></h2>
<p>One metric used by the WHO to determine the severity of global rates of coercive, forced sexual activity was the question "Have you ever been forced to have sexual intercourse against your will?" Asking this question produced higher positive response rates than being asked, whether they had ever been abused or raped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krug2002_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krug2002-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The WHO report describes the negative consequences of sexual abuse:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">
<ul>
<li>Gynecological disorders</li>
<li>Reproductive disorders</li>
<li>Sexual disorders</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Infertility" title="Infertility">Infertility</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pelvic_inflammatory_disease" title="Pelvic inflammatory disease">Pelvic inflammatory disease</a></li>
<li>Pregnancy complications</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">Miscarriage</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sexual_dysfunction" title="Sexual dysfunction">Sexual dysfunction</a></li>
<li>Acquiring <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infection" title="Sexually transmitted infection">sexually transmitted infections</a>, including HIV/AIDS</li>
<li>Mortality from injuries</li>
<li>Increased risk of <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">Depression</a></li>
<li>Chronic pain</li>
<li>Psychosomatic disorders</li>
<li>Unsafe abortion</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unwanted_pregnancy" title="Unwanted pregnancy">Unwanted pregnancy</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_from_rape" title="Pregnancy from rape">Pregnancy from rape</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krug2002_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Krug2002-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emotional_and_psychological">Emotional and psychological</span></h3>
<p>During the assault a person will generally act in one or more of five ways: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fight_or_flight_response" title="Fight or flight response">fight, flight</a>, freeze, friend, or flop; the way a person reacts is often not what he or she would have predicted, and after the rape is over, a rape survivor may be uncomfortable with and not understand how they reacted while it was occurring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Most people respond passively to the assault, which afterwards can cause confusion for people (including the survivor) who assume that someone being raped would call for help or struggle, resulting in their clothes being torn or there being injuries resulting from the survivor being subdued after resisting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> People being raped often <a href="/wiki/Dissociation_(psychology)" title="Dissociation (psychology)">dissociate</a> to some extent during the assault.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> Partly due to that, the memory of the experience will often be fragmented, especially immediately afterwards; memory generally consolidates with time, and especially following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/REM_sleep" title="REM sleep">REM sleep</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> A man or boy who is raped may get an erection and may ejaculate during the experience, and a woman or girl may orgasm during a sexual assault, which may become a source of shame and confusion for the person who was assaulted and people around him or her afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Male2013_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Male2013-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Immediately following a rape, the survivor may react outwardly in a wide range of ways, from expressive to closed down; common emotions include distress, anxiety, shame, revulsion, helplessness, and guilt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> Denial is not uncommon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-5"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the weeks following the rape, the survivor may develop symptoms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_traumatic_stress_syndrome" title="Post traumatic stress syndrome">post traumatic stress syndrome</a> and may develop wide array of psychosomatic complaints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-6"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2016_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2016-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:310</sup> PTSD symptoms include re-experiencing of the rape, avoiding things associated with the rape, numbness, and increased anxiety and <a href="/wiki/Startle_response" title="Startle response">startle response</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-7"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> The likelihood of sustained severe symptoms is higher if the rapist confined or restrained the person, if the person being raped believed the rapist would kill him or her, the person who was raped was very young or very old, and if the rapist was someone he or she knew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-8"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> The likelihood of sustained severe symptoms is also higher if people around the survivor ignore (or are ignorant of) the rape or blame the rape survivor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-9"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most people recover from rape in three to four months, but many have persistent PTSD that may manifest in anxiety, depression, substance abuse, irritability, anger, flashbacks, or nightmares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-10"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> In addition, rape survivors may have long term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalised_anxiety_disorder" title="Generalised anxiety disorder">generalised anxiety disorder</a>, may develop one or more <a href="/wiki/Specific_phobia" title="Specific phobia">specific phobias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>, and may experience difficulties with resuming their social life, and with sexual functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Psych2013rev_57-11"><a href="#cite_note-Psych2013rev-57">[57]</a></sup> People who have been raped are at higher risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Male2013_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Male2013-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Men experience similar psychological effects of being raped, but they are less likely to seek counseling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Male2013_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-Male2013-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another effect of rape and sexual assault is the stress created in those who study rape or counsel the survivors. This is called <a href="/wiki/Vicarious_traumatization" title="Vicarious traumatization">vicarious traumatization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical">Physical</span></h3>
<p>Rape and other sexual assault can result in physical trauma, tissue damage and infection, but most people will not suffer visible physical injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Undue importance is often placed on the presence or absence of physical injury when considering whether a rape occurred, in part because of old definitions of rape that were based on "use of force" rather than "lack of consent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> This stereotype can be damaging because people who have experienced sexual assault but have no physical trauma may be less inclined to report to the authorities or to seek health care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>While penetrative rape generally does not involve the use of a condom, in some cases a condom is used. This significantly reduces the likelihood of pregnancy and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disease_transmission" title="Disease transmission">disease transmission</a>, both to the victim and to the rapist. Rationales for condom use include: avoiding contracting infections or diseases (particularly <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>), especially in cases of rape of <a href="/wiki/Sex_worker" title="Sex worker">sex workers</a> or in gang rape (to avoid contracting infections or diseases from fellow rapists); eliminating evidence, making prosecution more difficult (and giving a sense of invulnerability); giving the appearance of consent (in cases of acquaintance rape); and thrill from planning and the use of the condom as an added prop.Concern for the victim is generally not considered a factor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-condom_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-condom-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexually_transmitted_infections">Sexually transmitted infections</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Virgin_cleansing_myth" title="Virgin cleansing myth">Virgin cleansing myth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prison_rape_in_the_United_States#Sexually_transmitted_diseases" title="Prison rape in the United States">Prison rape in the United States § Sexually transmitted diseases</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg/220px-Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg/330px-Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg/440px-Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Don%27t_Abuse_Children_sign_in_South_Africa.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A street sign in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, appealing to men not to rape children in the belief that it will cure them of HIV/AIDS.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cuts and abrasions acquired during the rape or sexual assault can become infected. Sexually transmitted infections (STI) can be <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(medicine)" title="Transmission (medicine)">transmitted</a> from the perpetrator to the victim. The presence of STIs in prepubescent children is an indicator of child sexual abuse. The risk of contracting an STI from being raped or sexually assaulted depends on a number of factors. The risk of infection is dependent upon the site of exposure, geographic region, the infection status of the perpetrator, and the type of assault. A pre-existing STI may be present in the patient.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Those who have been raped have relatively more reproductive tract infections than those who have not been raped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kimura_2013_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kimura_2013-69">[69]</a></sup> Trichomoniasis, bacterial vaginosis (BV), gonorrhea, and chlamydial infection are the most frequently diagnosed infections among sexually assaulted women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VAW2013_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-VAW2013-70">[70]</a></sup> Hepatitis B is sometimes acquired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cybulska2013_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cybulska2013-71">[71]</a></sup> The HIV virus can be transmitted through rape. Acquiring AIDS through rape puts people risk of suffering psychological problems. Acquiring HIV through rape may lead to the in behaviors that create risk of injecting drugs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Acquiring sexually transmitted infections also makes someone more likely to acquire HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kimura_2013_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kimura_2013-69">[69]</a></sup> In parts of Africa, there is a myth that sex with a <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">virgin</a> can cure HIV/AIDS; as such, girls and women are raped because of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cure_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-cure-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> It is not known how common the myth is and to what degree rapes happen because of the belief in it. The claim that the myth drives either HIV infection or child sexual abuse in South Africa is disputed by researchers <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Jewkes" title="Rachel Jewkes">Rachel Jewkes</a> and Helen Epstein.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Victim_blaming.2C_bullying_and_other_mistreatment">Victim blaming, bullying and other mistreatment</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Victim_blaming" title="Victim blaming">Victim blaming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-assault_treatment_of_sexual_assault_victims" title="Post-assault treatment of sexual assault victims">Post-assault treatment of sexual assault victims</a></div>
<p>People who have been raped or sexually assaulted are sometimes blamed and considered responsible for the crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maier2008_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Maier2008-17">[17]</a></sup> This concept refers to the <a href="/wiki/Just-world_hypothesis" title="Just-world hypothesis">just world fallacy</a> and attitudes that certain victim behaviors (such as <a href="/wiki/Flirting" title="Flirting">flirting</a> or wearing sexually <a href="/wiki/Provocation_(legal)" title="Provocation (legal)">provocative</a> clothing) may encourage rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In extreme cases, victims are said to have "asked for it" by not behaving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demure" title="Demure">demurely</a>. In most Western countries, the defense of provocation is not accepted as a mitigation for rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> A global survey of attitudes toward sexual violence by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Forum_for_Health_Research" title="Global Forum for Health Research">Global Forum for Health Research</a> shows that victim-blaming concepts are at least partially accepted in many countries. Women who have been raped are sometimes deemed to have behaved improperly. Often, these are countries where there is a significant social divide between the freedoms and status afforded to men and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Amy M. Buddie and Arthur G. Miller, in a review of studies of rape myths, state:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Rape victims are blamed more when they resist the attack later in the rape encounter rather than earlier (Kopper, 1996), which seems to suggest the stereotype that these women are engaging in token resistance (Malamuth &amp; Brown, 1994; Muehlenhard &amp; Rogers, 1998) or leading the man on because they have gone along with the sexual experience thus far. Finally, rape victims are blamed more when they are raped by an acquaintance or a date rather than by a stranger (e.g., Bell, Kuriloff, &amp; Lottes, 1994; Bridges, 1991; Bridges &amp; McGr ail, 1989; Check &amp; Malamuth, 1983; Kanekar, Shaherwalla, Franco, Kunju, &amp; Pinto, 1991; L'Armand &amp; Pepitone, 1982; Tetreault &amp; Barnett, 1987), which seems to evoke the stereotype that victims really want to have sex because they know their attacker and perhaps even went out on a date with him. The underlying message of this research seems to be that when certain stereotypical elements of rape are in place, rape victims are prone to being blamed.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>They also state that "individuals may endorse rape myths and at the same time recognize the negative effects of rape."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> A number of <a href="/wiki/Gender_role" title="Gender role">gender role</a> stereotypes can play a role in rationalization of rape. In the case of male-on-female rape, these include the idea that power is reserved to men whereas women are meant for sex and objectified, that women want forced sex and to be pushed around,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neumann_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-neumann-82">[82]</a></sup> and that male sexual impulses and behaviors are uncontrollable and must be satisfied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Victim-blaming correlates with fear. Many rape victims blame themselves. Female jurors might look at the woman on the witness stand and believe she has done something to entice the defendant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Victims may become the target of <a href="/wiki/Slut-shaming" title="Slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyberbullying" title="Cyberbullying">cyberbullying</a>. In addition, their credibility may be challenged.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Honor_killings_and_forced_marriages">Honor killings and forced marriages</span></h4>
<p>In many cultures, those who are raped are at very high risk of suffering additional violence or threats of violence after the rape. These acts may be perpetrated by the rapist or by friends and relatives of the rapist, as a way of preventing the victims from reporting the rape, of punishing them for reporting it, or of forcing them to withdraw the complaint; or they may be perpetrated by the relatives of the victim as a punishment for "bringing shame" to the family. This is especially the case in cultures where female virginity is highly valued and considered mandatory before marriage; in extreme cases, rape victims are killed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honor_killings" title="Honor killings">honor killings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zeenews.india_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-zeenews.india-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wisemuslimwomen_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-wisemuslimwomen-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In some places, girls and women who are raped are often forced by their families to marry their rapist. Because being the victim of rape and losing virginity carry extreme social stigma, and the victims are deemed to have their "reputation" tarnished, a marriage with the rapist is arranged. This is claimed to be in the advantage of both the victim—who does not remain unmarried and doesn't lose social status—and of the rapist, who avoids punishment. In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Suicide_of_Amina_Filali" title="Suicide of Amina Filali">suicide of a 16-year-old Moroccan girl</a>—who, after having been forced by her family to marry her rapist at the suggestion of the prosecutor, and who subsequently endured abuse by the rapist after they married—sparked protests from activists against the law which allows the rapist to marry the victim in order to escape criminal sanctions, and against this social practice which is common in Morocco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Treatment">Treatment</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="813" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG/400px-Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG/600px-Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG/800px-Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Non_genital_injuries_to_women_who_are_sexually_assaulted.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Non-genital injuries to women who are sexually assaulted</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Emergency rooms of many hospitals now employ sexual assault nurse/forensic examiners (SAN/FEs) with specific training to care for those who have experienced a rape or sexual assault. They are able to conduct a focussed medical-legal exam. If such a trained nurse is not available the emergency department has a sexual assault protocol that has been established for treatment and the collection of evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovchick2016_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Markovchick2016-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-genital_injuries">Non-genital injuries</span></h3>
<p>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_treatment" title="Medical treatment">medical response</a> to sexual assault is a complete assessment. This general assessment will prioritize the treatment of injuries by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emergency_room" title="Emergency room">emergency room</a> staff. The examiner is either specially trained to assess and treat those assaulted or follows protocols established to ensure privacy and best treatment practices. Informed consent is always required prior to treatment unless the person who was assaulted is unconscious, intoxicated or does not have the mental capacity to give consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovchick2016_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Markovchick2016-25">[25]</a></sup> Priorities governing the physical exam are the treatment of serious life-threatening emergencies and then a general and complete assessment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HockettSaucier2015_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-HockettSaucier2015-86">[86]</a></sup> Some physical injuries are readily apparent such as, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_bites" title="Human bites">bites</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYJH_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYJH-87">[87]</a></sup> broken teeth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovchick2016_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Markovchick2016-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swelling_(medical)" title="Swelling (medical)">swelling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bruising" title="Bruising">bruising</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laceration" title="Laceration">lacerations</a> and scratches. In more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Violent" title="Violent">violent</a> cases, the victim may need to have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gunshot_wounds" title="Gunshot wounds">gunshot wounds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Stab_wound" title="Stab wound">stab wounds</a> treated. The use of informed consent allows the person to regain a full sense of <a href="/wiki/Power_and_control_in_abusive_relationships" title="Power and control in abusive relationships">control</a> over the procedures. After the general assessment and treatment of serious injuries, treatment may include the use of additional diagnostic testing such as x-rays, CT or MRI scans and blood work. After the physical injuries are addressed and treatment has begun, then forensic examination proceeds along with the gathering of evidence that can be used to identify and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prosecute" title="Prosecute">prosecute</a> the perpetrator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovchick2016_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-Markovchick2016-25">[25]</a></sup> Such <a href="/wiki/Evidence" title="Evidence">evidence</a>-gathering is only done with the complete consent of the patient or the <a href="/wiki/Caregiver" title="Caregiver">caregivers</a> of the patient. At this point in the treatment, experienced <a href="/wiki/Counsel" title="Counsel">social support staff</a> are made available to the patient and family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>If the patient or the caregivers, (typically parents) agree, the medical team utilizes standardized sampling and testing usually referred to a "<a href="/wiki/Rape_kit" title="Rape kit">rape kit</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The patient is informed that submitting to the use of the rape kit does not <a href="/wiki/Obligation" title="Obligation">obligate</a> them to file <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criminal_charges" title="Criminal charges">criminal charges</a> against the perpetrator. The patient is discouraged from bathing or showering for the purpose of obtaining samples from his or her hair. The sooner that samples are obtained after the assault, the more likely that evidence is present in the sample and will provide valid results. Once the injuries of the patient have been treated and she or he is stabilized, the sample gathering will begin. Staff will encourage the presence of a rape/sexual assault counselor to provide an advocate and reassurance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some physical effects of the rape are not immediately apparent. Follow up examinations also assess the patient for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tension_headaches" title="Tension headaches">tension headaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(medical)" title="Fatigue (medical)">fatigue</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sleep_pattern_disturbances&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sleep pattern disturbances (page does not exist)">sleep pattern disturbances</a>, gastrointestinal irritability, chronic pelvic pain, menstrual pain or irregularity, pelvic inflammatory disease, multiple yeast infections, sexual dysfunction, premenstrual distress, fibromyalgia, vaginal discharge, vaginal itching, burning during urination, and generalized vaginal pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HockettSaucier2015_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-HockettSaucier2015-86">[86]</a></sup> Any victim with abrasions are immunized for tetanus if 5 years have elapsed since their last immunization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Varcarolis_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Varcarolis-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Women are typically offered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraceptive" title="Contraceptive">contraceptive</a> medications because about 5% of male-on-female rapes result in pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Varcarolis_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Varcarolis-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genital_injuries">Genital injuries</span></h3>
<p>A complete <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pelvic_exam" title="Pelvic exam">pelvic exam</a> for rape (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anal_rape" title="Anal rape">anal</a> and/or vaginal) is conducted. An <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">oral exam</a> is done if there have been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injurie" title="Injurie">injuries</a> to the mouth, teeth, gums or <a href="/wiki/Pharynx" title="Pharynx">pharynx</a>. Though the patient may have no complaints about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genital_pain" title="Genital pain">genital pain</a> signs of trauma can still be assessed. Prior to the complete bodily and genital exam, the patient is asked to undress, standing on a white sheet that collects any <a href="/wiki/Debris" title="Debris">debris</a> that may be in the clothing. The clothing and sheet are properly bagged and labeled along with other samples that can be removed from the body or clothing of the patient. Samples of <a href="/wiki/Fiber" title="Fiber">fibers</a>, mud, <a href="/wiki/Hair" title="Hair">hair</a>, leaves are gathered if present. Samples of <a href="/wiki/Body_fluid" title="Body fluid">fluids</a> are collected to determine the presence of the perpetrator's <a href="/wiki/Saliva" title="Saliva">saliva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semen" title="Semen">semen</a> that may be present in the patients mouth, <a href="/wiki/Vagina" title="Vagina">vagina</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rectum" title="Rectum">rectum</a>. A wood lamp is a device that can detect semen on the skin. Sometimes the victim has <a href="/wiki/Abrasion_(medical)" title="Abrasion (medical)">scratched</a> the perpetrator in defense and fingernail scrapings can be collected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Injuries to the genital areas can be swelling, lacerations, and bruising. Common genital injuries are <a href="/wiki/Rectal_pain" title="Rectal pain">anal injury</a>, labial abrasions, hymenal bruising, tears of the posterior <a href="/wiki/Frenulum_of_labia_minora" title="Frenulum of labia minora">fourchette</a> and fossa. Genital injuries are more prevalent in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-menopausal" title="Post-menopausal">post-menopausal</a> women and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prepubescent" title="Prepubescent">prepubescent</a> girls. Internal injuries to the <a href="/wiki/Cervix" title="Cervix">cervix</a> and vagina can be visualized using <a href="/wiki/Colposcopy" title="Colposcopy">colposcopy</a>. Using colposcopy has increased the detection of internal trauma from six percent to fifty-three percent. Genital injuries to children who have been raped or sexually assaulted differ in that the abuse may be on-going or it happened in the past after the injuries heal. <a href="/wiki/Scar" title="Scar">Scarring</a> is one sign of the sexual abuse of children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infections">Infections</span></h3>
<p>Sexually transmitted bacterial, viral and other infections, if diagnosed, are treated. This decision may be made by the clinician with prophylactic antibiotic treatment for <a href="/wiki/Vaginitis" title="Vaginitis">vaginitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonorrhea" title="Gonorrhea">gonorrhea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trichomoniasis" title="Trichomoniasis">trichomoniasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chlamydia_infection" title="Chlamydia infection">chlamydia</a>. Chlamydial and gonococcal infections in women are of particular concern due to the possibility of ascending infection. <a href="/wiki/Immunization" title="Immunization">Immunization</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hepatitis_B_vaccination" title="Hepatitis B vaccination">hepatitis B</a> is often considered. After prophylactic treatment is initiated, further testing is done to determine what other treatments may be necessary for other infections transmitted during the assault.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Varcarolis_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-Varcarolis-90">[90]</a></sup> These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Serum <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_B" title="Hepatitis B">hepatitis B</a> surface antigen assay</li>
<li>Microscopic evaluation of <a href="/wiki/Vaginal_discharge" title="Vaginal discharge">vaginal discharge</a> (saline wash and staining)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microbiological_culture" title="Microbiological culture">Cultures</a> for <a href="/wiki/Neisseria_gonorrhoeae" title="Neisseria gonorrhoeae">Neisseria gonorrhoeae</a> and Chlamydia trachomatis from each penetrated location</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Venereal_Disease_Research_Laboratory_test" title="Venereal Disease Research Laboratory test">Serum Venereal Disease Research Laboratory test</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Complete_blood_count" title="Complete blood count">CBC</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liver_function_tests" title="Liver function tests">Liver function tests</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Creatinine" title="Creatinine">Serum creatinine level</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment may include the administration of <a href="/wiki/Zidovudine" title="Zidovudine">Zidovudine</a>/<a href="/wiki/Lamivudine" title="Lamivudine">lamivudine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenofovir" title="Tenofovir">Tenofovir</a>/<a href="/wiki/Emtricitabine" title="Emtricitabine">emtricitabine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ritonavir" title="Ritonavir">Ritonavir</a>/<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lopinvir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lopinvir (page does not exist)">lopinvir</a>. Additional treatment options are available from the CDC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The transmission of HIV is frequently a major concern of the patient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VAW2013_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-VAW2013-70">[70]</a></sup> Prophylactic treatment for HIV is not necessarily administered. Routine treatment for HIV after rape or sexual assault is controversial due to the low risk of infection after one sexual assault. Transmission of HIV after one exposure to penetrative anal sex is estimated to be 0.5 to 3.2 percent. Transmission of HIV after one exposure to penetrative vaginal intercourse is 0.05 to 0.15 percent. HIV can also be contracted through the oral route but is considered rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-5"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Other recommendations are that the patient be treated prophylactically for HIV if the perpetrator is found to be infected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYJH_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYJH-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Testing at the time of the initial exam does not typically have forensic value if patients are sexually active and have an STI since it could have been acquired prior to the assault. Rape shield laws protect the person who was raped and who has positive test results. These laws prevent having such evidence used against someone who was raped. Someone who was raped may be concerned that a prior infection may suggest sexual promiscuity. There may, however, be situations in which testing has the legal purpose, as in cases where the threat of transmission or actual transmission of an STI was part of the crime. In nonsexually active patients, an initial, baseline negative test that is followed by a subsequent STI could be used as evidence, if the perpetrator also had an STI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VAW2013_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-VAW2013-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Treatment failure is possible due to the emergence of antibiotic-resistant strains of pathogens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaardaSikora2015_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-BaardaSikora2015-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emotional_and_psychiatric">Emotional and psychiatric</span></h3>
<p>Psychiatric and emotional consequences can be apparent immediately after rape and it may be necessary to treat these very early in the evaluation and treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VAW2013_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-VAW2013-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other treatable emotional and psychiatric disorders may not become evident after the rape. These can be <a href="/wiki/Eating_disorder" title="Eating disorder">eating</a> disorders, anxiety, fear, intrusive thoughts, fear of crowds, avoidance, anger, depression, humiliation, post-traumatic stress disorder (PTSD) hyperarousal, sexual disorders,(including fear of engaging in sexual activity), mood disorders, suicidal ideation, borderline personality disorder, nightmares, fear of situations that remind the patient of the rape and fear of being alone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HockettSaucier2015_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-HockettSaucier2015-86">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Psychomotor_agitation" title="Psychomotor agitation">agitation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Numbness" title="Numbness">numbness</a> and emotional distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-6"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup> Victims are able to receive help by using a telephone hotline, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counseling" title="Counseling">counseling</a>, or shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosdahl_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rosdahl-33">[33]</a></sup> Recovery from sexual assault is a complicated and controversial concept,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Recovering_from_sexual_assault_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Recovering_from_sexual_assault-93">[93]</a></sup> but support groups, usually accessed by <a href="/wiki/List_of_anti-sexual_assault_organizations_in_the_United_States" title="List of anti-sexual assault organizations in the United States">organizations</a> are available to help in recovery. Professional counseling and on-going treatment by trained health care providers is often sought by the victim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bud2015_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bud2015-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are clinicians who are specially trained in the treatment of those who have experienced rape and sexual assault/abuse. Treatment can be lengthy and be challenging for both the counselor and the patient. Several treatment options exist and vary by accessibility, cost, or whether or not insurance coverage exists for the treatment. Treatment also varies dependent upon the expertise of the counselor—some have more experience and or have specialized in the treatment of sexual trauma and rape. To be the most effective, a treatment plan should developed based upon the struggles of the patient and not necessarily based upon the traumatic experience. An effective treatment plan will take the following into consideration: current stressors, coping skills, physical health, interpersonal conflicts, self-esteem, family issues, involvement of the guardian, and the presence of mental health symptoms. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bud2015_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bud2015-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The degree of success for emotional and psychiatric treatments is often dependent upon the terminology used in the treatment, i.e. redefining the event and experience. Labels used like "rape victim" and "rape survivor" to describe the new identities of women who have been raped suggest that the event is the dominant and controlling influence on her life. These may have an effect on supportive personnel. The consequences of using these labels needs to be assessed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HockettSaucier2015_86-3"><a href="#cite_note-HockettSaucier2015-86">[86]</a></sup> Positive outcomes of emotional and psychiatric treatment for rape exist; these can be an improved self-concept, the recognition of growth, and implementing new coping styles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HockettSaucier2015_86-4"><a href="#cite_note-HockettSaucier2015-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>A perpetrator found guilty by the court is often required to receive treatment. There are many options for treatment, some more successful than others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The psychological factors that motivated the convicted perpetrator are complex but treatment can still be effective. A counselor will typically evaluate disorders that are currently present in the offender. Investigating the developmental background of the offender can help explain the origins of the abusive behavior occurred in the first place. Emotional and psychological treatment has the purpose of identifying predictors of recidivism, or the potential that the offender will commit rape again. In some instances neurological abnormalities have been identified in the perpetrators, and in some cases they have themselves experienced past trauma. Adolescents and other children can be the perpetrators of rape, although this is uncommon. In this instance, appropriate counseling and evaluation are usually conducted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelly2011_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kelly2011-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Short-term treatment with a <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepine</a> may help with anxiety and antidepressants may be helpful for symptoms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PTSD" title="PTSD">post traumatic stress disorder</a>, depression and panic attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Varcarolis_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-Varcarolis-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evidence_collection">Evidence collection</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rape_investigation" title="Rape investigation">Rape investigation</a></div>
<p>Though technically, medical staff are not part of the legal system, only trained medical personnel can obtain evidence that is admissible during a trial. The procedures have been standardized. Evidence is collected, signed, and locked in a secure place to guarantee that legal evidence procedures are maintained. This is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chain_of_evidence" title="Chain of evidence">chain of evidence</a> and is a legal term that describes a carefully monitored procedure of evidence collection and preservation. Maintaining the Chain of evidence from the medical examination, testing and <a href="/wiki/Tissue_(biology)" title="Tissue (biology)">tissue</a> sampling from its origin of collection to court allows the results of the sampling to be admitted as evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_88-7"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-88">[88]</a></sup> The use of photography is often used for documentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VAW2013_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-VAW2013-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The information derived from the analysis can often help determine whether sexual contact occurred, providing information regarding the circumstances of the incident, and be compared to reference samples collected from patients and suspects.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">Prevention</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Initiatives_to_prevent_sexual_violence" title="Initiatives to prevent sexual violence">Initiatives to prevent sexual violence</a></div>
<p>As sexual violence affects all parts of society, the response to sexual violence is comprehensive. The responses can be categorized as: individual approaches, health care responses, community-based efforts and actions to prevent other forms of sexual violence.</p>
<p>Sexual assault may be prevented by <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> college,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foubert_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foubert-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and workplace education programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> At least one program for <a href="/wiki/Fraternity" title="Fraternity">fraternity</a> men produced "sustained behavioral change."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foubert_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Foubert-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_and_epidemiology">Statistics and epidemiology</span></h2>
<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG"><img alt="Rape perpetrator pie chart.PNG" data-file-height="503" data-file-width="713" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG/350px-Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG/525px-Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG/700px-Rape_perpetrator_pie_chart.PNG 2x" width="350"/></a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rape_statistics" title="Rape statistics">Rape statistics</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Estimates_of_sexual_violence" title="Estimates of sexual violence">Estimates of sexual violence</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide">Worldwide</span></h3>
<p>International Crime on Statistics and Justice by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> (UNODC) find that worldwide, most victims of rape are women and most perpetrators male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">[101]</a></sup> The study also found that rapes against women are rarely reported to the police and that the number of female rape victims is significantly underestimated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">[101]</a></sup> Southern Africa, Oceania and North America also report the highest records of rape rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most rape research and reports of rape are limited to male-female forms of rape. Research on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Male_rape" title="Male rape">male-on-male and female-on-male rape</a> is rare. Fewer than one in ten male-male rapes are reported. As a group, males who have been raped by either gender often get little services and support, and legal systems are often ill equipped to deal with this type of crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc.net.au_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc.net.au-102">[102]</a></sup> Instances in which the perpetrator is female, are not clear and lead to the denial of women being sexual aggressors. This could obscure the true dimensions of the problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denov_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denov-103">[103]</a></sup> It is likely under-reported illustrating a double standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malesrapingfemales_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-malesrapingfemales-104">[104]</a></sup> Forty-three percent of high school and young college men reported being coerced into sexual behavior and, of those, 95% reported that a female was the aggressor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rape_Rate.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="563" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rape_Rate.png/350px-Rape_Rate.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rape_Rate.png/525px-Rape_Rate.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Rape_Rate.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rape_Rate.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UNODC : Reported rape per 100,000 population (2011)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The humanitarian news organization <a href="/wiki/IRIN" title="IRIN">IRIN</a> claims that an estimated "500,000 rapes are committed annually in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> once called 'the world's rape capital.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The country has some of the highest incidences of child sexual abuse in the world with more than 67,000 cases of rape and sexual assaults against children reported in 2000, with welfare groups believing that unreported incidents could be up to 10 times higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cure_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-cure-73">[73]</a></sup> Current data suggest that the incidence of rape has risen significantly in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SharmaSrivastava2015_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-SharmaSrivastava2015-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rape_in_the_United_States" title="Rape in the United States">Rape in the United States</a></div>
